The two tone dark outer and light inner wings were easily visible.  not uniform color like the juvenile Black crowned night heron. It had a dark streak that extended from the eye area.   It was comparatively larger than the nearby black crowned nith herons.   We were near the tennis courts that used to have a fence around them.  It is in back of the restaurant and good viewing of the marsh.  We were calling for sora's and rails when this bird took flight and gave its course bass flight call.  it flew about 50 yards and ducked into the reeds.  At one time in flight it extended its neck and it was much longer than a black crowned night heron.  this area has warm spring waters that seem to keep the rails, ducks and other species around.

Approx count. Many individs. scattered across the entire refuge. The size of the birds were larger than BCNHs with longer necks and bold, solid parallel/vertical striping down the underside of the neck, as opposed to the short streaking of juvenile BCNHs. The AMBIs also had dark primaries, primary coverts, and secondaries, contrasting with the light brown lesser coverts and back feathers. We identified some BCNHs, but there were very few throughout the reserve.

URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS56293065	2017-04-18 17:05:33	7052	species	American Bittern	Botaurus lentiginosus			1				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Nye	US-NV-023	US-NV_977	33	USFWS_350		Ash Meadows NWR HQ	L388900	H	36.4204294	-116.3299853	1965-04-14	06:15:00	obsr56422	S4058241	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	405	4.023	4.0469	2	1		0	1	0		Potash Springs, Longstreet Springs, Frog Springs and Rodgers Springs. Habitat varies, see bird notes. 55F, warm, sunny. This is a Desert Ecology Class, Chico State College. We are in the northern end of Ash Meadows in western Nevada. It is a hot, arid land with steep rising mountains which almost totally lack any type of vegetation. Potash Springs, one mile north of Longstreet Springs was where we camped. The springs are an oasis in the desert. Vegetation is very sparse and located primarily around these springs. Plants are Tamarisk, willow, cottonwood,  and some sedges. Away from water the basic shrubs are Mesquite. Some succulents and Creosote present. Buildings at the various sights were built around 1860. Potash Springs is approx. 4 miles west of SR29 and about 10 miles south of Lathrop Wells, NV. Frog Springs and Rodger Springs are located inbetween Potash and Longstreet Springs.----Observers: Myself and Dr. Dempsey----Footnote: 8PM, Lou Davis and I went north 19 miles to some sand dunes. Only insect present were 3 beetles, some grubs and 5 Dune Crickets. These crickets never before found this far north. All beetles proceeding up dunes, none down.
